URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS504483765	2019-05-08 07:43:46	32906	species	Kentucky Warbler	Geothlypis formosa			1					United States	US	Michigan	US-MI	Alger	US-MI-003					Pictured Rocks NL - Sand Point	L4661843	P	46.4513471	-86.6069906	2017-05-25	09:13:00	obsr196130	S37137961	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	67	2.816		1	1		0	1	1			I observed this bird as it was moving along the edge of the road through thick brush underlying trees interspersed with sections of shrubless floodings where Northern Waterthrushes were singing.  It was an unmarked green khaki dorsally.  All sections of the ventral surfaces that I could see were yellow (throat, lower breast, and belly) and also unmarked.   The intersection of the lateral face with the chin and throat was bordered by a black triangular patch that was widest at its "start" from the base of the eye and narrowed as it descended.  It exhibited easily discernible yellow spectacles.  The most likely alternative would be Canada Warbler, but I had just observed this species and the bird in question was immediately perceptible as "different".  First, its dorsal surfaces were a greenish color, not a slightly bluish gray.  Secondly, the black border of the lateral lower face with the chin and throat were larger and bolder than in Canada Warbler, and lastly, it had yellow spectacles, not a yellowish supraloral connecting to a complete and distinct whitish eye ring.

This bird was silent and luckily I was able to spot it in a thicket of low vegetation.  The bright yellow eyebrow that wraps partway behind the eye gives a spectacled look.  The bird had a black almost triangular cheeck patch that extended down the neck and a dark crown that is gray toward the rear, bright yellow throat and underparts, and is olive green on top.  There were no wing-bars and no tail-spots were evident on the short tail.  The dark bill was short and fairly stout.--The similar sized common yellowthroat has a black mask with a whitish border on top.  Hooded warbler male has a black hood with a yellow face with white tail spots.  Canada warbler has a black necklace and is gray on top with a bold whitish or yellowish eye-ring.

Historical breeding spot for Kentucky warblers; among others Alan has found Kentuckys in this location since 2004.  Two birds observed and heard; third one heard only.  Olive-backed, bright yellow below; black mask trailing down side of neck to breast; yellow spectacles; short tail. Vocalized with loud, steady, repeated pur-reets; tone more musical and less staccato than ovenbird and without the crescendo toward the end of the song.  Chuck calls also heard. Good weather although a bit variable. Mostly calm conditions.	An overshoot migrant, heard once then seen off and on for ~2 minutes as it foraged in a brushy tangle.  Warbler with a yellow underside, olive-green back, no wing bars.  Facial markings were diagnostic with a bright yellow supercilium over the eye and then hooking back behind the eye in a thin crescent.  Classic black marking from just in front of the eye, extending under the eye, and down to the shoulder.  Certainly not a Common Yellowthroat as the warbler lacked the black mask bordered by gray-white margin.  Due to the brushy tangle, I was unable to take a photo but I am very familiar with this species and have photographed it in the past.

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS609931307	2021-04-01 07:52:31.80637	32906	species	Kentucky Warbler	Geothlypis formosa			1					United States	US	Michigan	US-MI	Kent	US-MI-081		23			Huff Park	L613092	H	43.0058000	-85.6349800	2018-05-03	13:13:00	obsr924746	S45224154	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	141	3.219		1	1		0	1	1			Extremely rare for Kent county,  only second report.  ----Very yellow overall,  black cap,  and very distinct black triangular cheek patch.  Wilson's Warbler does not have the cheek patch,  Common Yellowthroat (which was in the area) has a black mask across the face unlike this,  and Hooded Warbler has a full hood.  Thin line of yellow between the face patch and mask gave the bird its distinct "spectacles".  ----I was at the lone picnic table near the far in outlet of boardwalk (NOT Aberdeen) and was eyeing a couple of Ovenbirds and saw many more small birds flitting away in the brush inside the woods.  So I ventured out into the woods.  There is no distinct path,  but I eventually hit a more open area (circular open area) with heavy brush on either side.  It was very muddy and flooded.  It is on the edge of the stream that runs under the bridge on the far in outlet.  There was a large mud puddle.  Very thick brush,  the warbler was hopping in the brush,  briefly coming out.  Time spent in the open was never more than 5 seconds.  Eventually he flew away (after about 2 minutes of viewing) in direction of flooded woodland on boardwalk.  I ventured out to find him and couldn't relocate.  I do not have pictures,  I couldn't find him in my optical viewfinder.  He did not vocalize.  I am very confident with this identification,  I ruled out the species I feel could be mistaken for him.

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS765856758	2019-06-05 09:04:52	32906	species	Kentucky Warbler	Geothlypis formosa			1					United States	US	Michigan	US-MI	Leelanau	US-MI-089	US-MI_2900	12			Tucker Lake	L9083325	H	44.9034317	-85.9548532	2019-05-25	11:29:00	obsr350470	S56718895	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	60	0.241		2	1		0	1	1			Two of us were in our car as we were just about to leave. We were parked on the north side of the little parking lot and I was sitting in the passenger seat with my window down looking into brushy area next to the car. A small warbler-size bird flew out from low in the dense bushes and tangles, then landed on a fallen log about 15 feet from me. I had a full, unobstructed, profile view — with decent lighting — of the entire bird for about 3 seconds before it continued on its way, staying low and looking like it was going to land on the ground. I immediately recognized it as a Kentucky Warbler.--We spent about 20 minutes trying to find it again but ran out of time and left without relocating it.--It was bright yellow below and dark olive above showing no wing bars or or other white markings. Yellow throat and yellow supercillium which wrapped around the back of the eye but not a complete eye-ring like the CAWA (also did not see a black necklace or white coverts or white under the wing when it flew). Distinctive black facial pattern on the cheek which continued down the side of the yellow throat to the breast. --R/O WIWA black cap but no black facial pattern, yellow face with faint olive cheek, small. R/O immature HOWA no black on head or facial pattern. R/O COYE Black face, no yellow supercillium.--Last week I saw my first KEWA at Tawas Point. I had a lengthy and very close-up view, watching as it casually walked on the ground under the bushes. I was surprised how impressive looking he was with his long legs and beautiful facial pattern which stands out even in the shade of the bushes.
